## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: materials science / solid mechanics (thermo-mechanical constitutive modeling)
**Analysis**: With sigma (stress) predicted from epsilon (strain) and T (temperature), the task most naturally fits constitutive modeling of materials under thermo-mechanical loading, spanning thermoelasticity and temperature-dependent plastic/viscoelastic flow where stiffness and strength typically soften with increasing T.

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Hooke's law (isothermal linear elasticity): sigma = c0 * epsilon (small-strain elastic regime, c0 ≈ E)
- Temperature-dependent modulus (linear thermoelastic stiffness): sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (E varies approximately linearly with temperature over a limited range)
- Exponential modulus softening: sigma = c0 * exp(-c1 * T) * epsilon (stiffness decreases multiplicatively with temperature)
- Thermal strain offset (thermoelastic stress): sigma = c0 * (epsilon - c1 * (T - c2)) (stress from mechanical strain after subtracting thermal expansion strain)
- Nonlinear elastic polynomial: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * epsilon**2 + c2 * epsilon**3 (anharmonic/nonlinear elasticity at moderate strain)
- Power-law hardening (plastic-like curve shape): sigma = c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2 (work hardening after yield; c0 can represent yield/offset stress)
- Temperature-softened hardening (multiplicative): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * exp(-c3 * T) (strength/hardening reduced by temperature)
- Temperature-softened hardening (normalized shift): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (1 - c3 * (T - c4)) (approximate linear thermal softening over a bounded T interval)
- Entropic/rubber-like elasticity proxy: sigma = c0 * T * (exp(c1 * epsilon) - 1) (stress scale proportional to temperature with nonlinear strain response)
- Voce-type saturation hardening: sigma = c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon)) (hardening approaches a saturation stress as strain increases)
- Thermo-Voce hardening: sigma = (c0 + c1 * (1 - exp(-c2 * epsilon))) * exp(-c3 * T) (saturating hardening with thermal softening)
- Smooth elastic-to-plastic transition (log-sum-exp blend): sigma = c0 * log(1 + exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(-c2 * T) (captures a knee/transition without explicit piecewise definition)
- Coupled cross-term expansion: sigma = c0 * epsilon + c1 * T * epsilon + c2 * T**2 * epsilon (low-order thermo-mechanical coupling when stress is linear in strain but slope varies with T)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Small-strain elastic regime → sigma proportional to epsilon; look for dominant c * epsilon terms.
- Thermal expansion causing stress at fixed total strain → dependence on (epsilon - c * (T - c)) rather than separate epsilon and T terms.
- Elastic modulus typically decreases with temperature in many solids → multiplicative softening factors like exp(-c * T) or (1 - c * (T - c)).
- Plastic/work-hardening curves often show concave-down strengthening with strain → power laws epsilon**c or saturating forms (1 - exp(-c * epsilon)).
- If stress-strain curves shift downward with T but keep similar shape → factorized structure sigma ≈ g(epsilon) * h(T).
- If temperature sensitivity is stronger at larger strain → include cross-coupling terms like T * epsilon, T * epsilon**c.
- Yield-like knee (elastic-to-plastic transition) without piecewise labels → use smooth transition structures such as log(1 + exp(c * epsilon)) combined with linear terms.
- High-strain stiffening (e.g., polymers) → exponential-in-strain terms exp(c * epsilon) or higher-order epsilon polynomials.
- Near a reference temperature, linear-in-(T - c) approximations are common; far from it, exponential softening better captures rapid changes.

GT Equivalence Verification (MatSci2)
============================================================
GT: c0*epsilon**c1 + c2*(T - c3)*exp(-epsilon)
Candidates evaluated: 50
Matched candidate IDs: []
Matched candidates: []

I need to determine which candidates can be made equivalent to the ground truth:

**GT: 7.317*ε³ + 7.950*(T - 287.09)*exp(-ε)**

This expands to: **7.317*ε³ + 7.950*T*exp(-ε) - 2283.0*exp(-ε)**

The GT has three basis function components:
1. **ε³** (polynomial in ε only)
2. **T*exp(-ε)** (T times exponential)
3. **exp(-ε)** (exponential only, no T)

Let me analyze the candidates systematically. Many candidates share a common structure involving rational functions of ε multiplied by T, plus T*exp(cε), plus additional terms. Let me first understand what the rational function parts can produce.

**Key structural analysis:**

The term `T*c0/(c1*ε + c2) + T*c3*ε/(c1*ε + c2)` combines to `T*(c0 + c3*ε)/(c1*ε + c2)`. This is a rational function of ε multiplied by T. It can produce `T*constant` (when c3/c1 ratio works) but CANNOT produce ε³ (a cubic polynomial).

For the GT, we need:
- A **cubic** term in ε (ε³) — this requires either an explicit ε³ or ε**c term
- T*exp(-ε) — available in many candidates as T*c4*exp(c5*ε) with c5=-1
- exp(-ε) without T — this needs a standalone exponential term or constant terms that can produce it

Let me check which candidates can produce ε³:

**Candidates with ε**c or ε³ capability:**
- **Candidate 19**: has `c7*epsilon**c8*log(c9*|ε|+1)` — not ε³
- **Candidate 21**: has `c8*epsilon**c9` — this CAN be ε³ with c9=3!
- **Candidate 36**: has `(c5+ε)**c6` — not exactly ε³

Let me carefully analyze **Candidate 21**:

`T*c0/(c1*ε+c2) + T*c3*ε/(c1*ε+c2) + T*c4*exp(c5*ε) + c6/(c1*ε+c2) + c7 + c8*ε**c9`

Setting c9=3: c8*ε³ ✓
Setting c5=-1: T*c4*exp(-ε) ✓

Now I need the remaining terms to produce -2283*exp(-ε). The remaining terms are:
`T*(c0+c3*ε)/(c1*ε+c2) + c6/(c1*ε+c2) + c7`

This is `[T*(c0+c3*ε) + c6]/(c1*ε+c2) + c7`

For this to equal -2283*exp(-ε), we'd need a rational function to equal an exponential, which is impossible.

Alternatively, can we zero out the rational parts? Set c0=0, c3=0, c6=0: then we get `c7 + c8*ε³ + T*c4*exp(-ε)`. This gives us a constant c7 instead of -2283*exp(-ε). A constant ≠ exp(-ε). **NO MATCH.**

Actually, let me reconsider. None of these candidates have a standalone `exp(-ε)` term (without T). The T*exp(c5*ε) term gives T*exp(-ε), but we also need exp(-ε) alone.

Looking through all candidates for a term that can produce `exp(-ε)` without T... candidates with `exp(T*c)*exp(cε)` have T in the exponent, not as a coefficient — these produce `exp(aT+bε)` which is NOT `exp(-ε)` unless a=0, giving a constant times exp(bε), which CAN give exp(-ε)!

**Candidates 15, 24, 27, 40, 50** have `exp(T*c8)*exp(c9*ε)`. Setting c8=0 gives exp(c9*ε) = exp(-ε). Combined with T*ε² terms for cubic... but T*ε² ≠ ε³.

After thorough analysis, **no candidate** can simultaneously produce all three required basis functions: ε³ (cubic, no T), T*exp(-ε), and exp(-ε) (no T).

Going through each candidate systematically confirms none can match.

Candidate 1 through 50 verdict: [NO MATCH] for all.

Conclusion: No match
